           <div class="publication-abstract" data-reactid="69">
            <div class="nova-e-text nova-e-text--size-xl nova-e-text--family-sans-serif nova-e-text--spacing-xs" data-reactid="70">
             Abstract
            </div>
            <div class="nova-e-text nova-e-text--size-m nova-e-text--family-sans-serif nova-e-text--spacing-auto" data-reactid="71">
             TIGER/Line shapefiles from the United States Census Bureau are commonly used for the mapping and analysis of US demographic trends. The tigris package provides a uniform interface for R users to download and work with these shapefiles. Functions in tigris allow R users to request Census geographic datasets using familiar geographic identifiers and return those datasets as objects of class Spatial*DataFrame. In turn, tigris ensures consistent and high-quality spatial data for R users’ cartographic and spatial analysis projects that involve US Census data. This article provides an overview of the functionality of the tigris package, and concludes with an applied example of a geospatial workflow using data retrieved with tigris.
            </div>
           </div>

            <div id="pf1" class="pf w0 h0" data-page-no="1">
             <div class="pc pc1 w0 h0">
              <div class="bi x0 y0 w1 h1" data-bg="profile/Kyle_Walker5/publication/308288744/viewer/AS:407972971859976@1474279744999/background/1.png" style="background-size: contain;"></div>
              <div class="t m0 x0 h2 y1 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls0">
               C
               <span class="fs1 ls1 ws0">ONTRIBUTED RESEARCH ARTICLE<span class="_ _0"> </span></span>
               <span class="ls6">1</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h3 y2 ff2 fs2 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               tigris:
               <span class="_ _1"> </span>An R Package to Access and W
               <span class="_ _2"></span>ork
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h3 y3 ff2 fs2 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               with Geographic Data from the US
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h3 y4 ff2 fs2 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               Census Bureau
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h4 y5 ff3 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               by Kyle Walker
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h5 y6 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               Abstract
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x2 h6 y6 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1">
               TIGER/Line shape?les from the United States Census Bureau are commonly used for the
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y7 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws2">
               mapping and analysis of US demographic trends. The
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x3 h5 y7 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x4 h6 y7 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws2">
               package provides a uniform interface
              </div>
              <div class="t m2 x1 h6 y8 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws3">
               for R users to download and work with these shape?les. Functions in
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x5 h5 y8 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m2 x6 h6 y8 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws3">
               allow R users to request
              </div>
              <div class="t m3 x1 h6 y9 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4">
               Census geographic datasets using familiar geographic identi?ers and return those datasets as objects
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 ya ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws5">
               of class
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x7 h7 ya ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               Spatial*DataFrame
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x8 h6 ya ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws5">
               .
               <span class="_ _3"> </span>In turn,
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x9 h5 ya ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 xa h6 ya ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws5">
               ensures consistent and high-quality spatial data for R
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 yb ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws6">
               users’ cartographic and spatial analysis projects that involve US Census data. This article provides
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 yc ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws3">
               an overview of the functionality of the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 xb h5 yc ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 xc h6 yc ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws3">
               package, and concludes with an applied example of a
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 yd ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               geospatial work?ow using data retrieved with 
               <span class="ff2 ws7">tigris</span>.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h8 ye ff2 fs5 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               Introduction
              </div>
              <div class="t m4 x1 h6 yf ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws6">
               Analysis and visualization of geographic data are often core components of the analytical work?ow
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y10 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws8">
               for researchers and data scientists; as such, access to open and reliable geographic datasets are of
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y11 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4">
               paramount importance. The United States Census Bureau provides access to such data in the form
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y12 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws9">
               of its TIGER/Line shape?le products (
               <span class="fc1">United States Census Bureau</span>
               <span class="ls2">,</span>
               <span class="fc1">2016a</span>).
               <span class="_ _4"> </span>The ?les are extracts
              </div>
              <div class="t m5 x1 h6 y13 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsa">
               from the Census Bureau’s Master Address File/T
               <span class="_ _2"></span>opologically Integrated Geographic Encoding and
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 y14 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsb">
               Referencing (TIGER) database, which in turn are released to the public as shape?les, a common format
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y15 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsc">
               for encoding geographic data as vectors (e.g. points, lines, and polygons).
               <span class="_ _4"> </span>Available TIGER/Line
              </div>
              <div class="t m7 x1 h6 y16 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsd">
               shape?les include all of the Census Bureau’s areal enumeration units, such as states, counties, Census
              </div>
              <div class="t m8 x1 h6 y17 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsa">
               tracts, and Census blocks; transportation data such as roads and railways; and both linear and areal
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 y18 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wse">
               hydrography
               <span class="_ _2"></span>.
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>The TIGER/Line ?les are updated annually
               <span class="_ _2"></span>, and include attributes that allow them to be
              </div>
              <div class="t m9 x1 h6 y19 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               joined with other tabular data, including demographic data products released by the Census Bureau.
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 xd h6 y1a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               The
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x7 h5 y1a ff2 fs3 fc1 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 xe h6 y1a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               package aims to simplify the process of working with these datasets for R users (
               <span class="fc1 ws7">W<span class="_ _2"></span>alker<span class="fc0">,</span></span>
              </div>
              <div class="t ma x1 h6 y1b ff1 fs3 fc1 sc0 ls6">
               2016
               <span class="fc0 wsd">). With functions in</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 xf h5 y1b ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t ma x10 h6 y1b ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsd">
               , R users can specify the data type and geography for which they would
              </div>
              <div class="t mb x1 h6 y1c ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4">
               like to obtain geographic data, and return the corresponding TIGER/Line data as an R object of class
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 y1d ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               Spatial*DataFrame
              </div>
              <div class="t mc x11 h6 y1d ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               . This article provides an overview of the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x12 h5 y1d ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t mc x13 h6 y1d ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4">
               package, and gives examples that
              </div>
              <div class="t mc x1 h6 y1e ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsf">
               show how it can contribute to common geographic visualization and spatial analysis work?ows in R.
              </div>
              <div class="t m4 x1 h6 y1f ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws6">
               Examples in the article include a discussion of how
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x14 h5 y1f ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m4 x15 h6 y1f ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws6">
               helps R users retrieve and work with data
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y20 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws10">
               from the US Census Bureau, as well as an applied example of how
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x16 h5 y20 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x17 h6 y20 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws11">
               can ?t within a common
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 y21 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws12">
               geospatial work?ow in R, in which data from the United States Internal Revenue Service are visualized
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y22 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               with both static and interactive cartography
               <span class="_ _2"></span>.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h8 y23 ff2 fs5 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               Geographic data and Census visualization in R
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y24 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws13">
               The TIGER/Line ?les were ?rst released by the US Census Bureau in ASCII format in 1989, and
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y25 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws14">
               represented street centerline data for the entire United States.
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>Since then,
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>the Census Bureau has
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y26 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws15">
               expanded the coverage of the TIGER/Line data, and transitioned the core format of the publicly-
              </div>
              <div class="t ma x1 h9 y27 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsd">
               available ?les to the shape?le in 2007. TIGER/Line shape?les include 
               <span class="ff3">boundary ?les</span>, which encompass
              </div>
              <div class="t md x1 h6 y28 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1">
               the boundaries of governmental units or other areal units for which the Census Bureau tabulates data.
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 y29 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws16">
               This includes the core Census hierarchy of areal units from the Census block (analogous to a city block)
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 y2a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws17">
               to the entire United States, as well as common geographic entities such as city boundaries. The Census
              </div>
              <div class="t me x1 h9 y2b ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsa">
               Bureau distinguishes between 
               <span class="ff3 ws6">legal entities<span class="ff1">, which have of?cial government standing, and </span>statistical</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h9 y2c ff3 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws7">
               entities
               <span class="ff1 ws18">, which have no legal de?nition but are used for the tabulation of data.<span class="_ _5"> </span>The Census Bureau</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t mc x1 h9 y2d ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsf">
               also makes available shape?les of 
               <span class="ff3">geographic features</span>, which include entities such as roads, rivers, and
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y2e ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws19">
               railroads.
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>All TIGER/Line shape?les are distributed in a geographic coordinate system using the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y2f ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               North American Datum of 1983 (NAD83) (
               <span class="fc1">United States Census Bureau</span>
               <span class="ls3">,</span>
               <span class="fc1">2014</span>).
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 xd h6 y30 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1a">
               As the TIGER/Line datasets are available in shape?le format, they can be read into and translated to
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 y31 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1b">
               R objects by the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x18 h5 y31 ff2 fs3 fc1 sc0 ls6">
               rgdal
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x19 h6 y31 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1b">
               package (
               <span class="fc1">Bivand et al.</span>
               <span class="ls4">,</span>
               <span class="fc1">2015</span>). rgdal is an R interface to the open-sourced Geospa-
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 y32 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1c">
               tial Data Abstraction Library
               <span class="_ _2"></span>, or GDAL, an open-source translator that can convert between numerous
              </div>
              <div class="t m9 x1 h6 y33 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               common vector and raster spatial data formats (
               <span class="fc1">GDAL Development T<span class="_ _2"></span>eam<span class="fc0 ls3">,</span>2015<span class="fc0">).<span class="_ _5"> </span>When loaded into</span></span>
              </div>
              <div class="t mf x1 h6 y34 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1d">
               R, shape?les will be represented as objects of class
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1a h7 y34 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               Spatial*
              </div>
              <div class="t mf x12 h6 y34 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsa">
               by the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1b h5 y34 ff2 fs3 fc1 sc0 ls6">
               sp
              </div>
              <div class="t mf x1c h6 y34 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1d">
               package (
               <span class="fc1">Bivand et al.</span>
               <span class="ls5">,</span>
               <span class="fc1">2013</span>).
              </div>
              <div class="t m7 x1 h6 y35 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsd">
               Most Census datasets obtained by
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1d h5 y35 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m7 x1e h6 y35 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsd">
               will be loaded as objects of class
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1f h7 y35 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               SpatialPolygonsDataFrame
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h2 y36 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               The R Journal V
               <span class="_ _2"></span>ol.
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>XX/YY, AAAA 20ZZ
               <span class="_ _6"> </span>ISSN 2073-4859

               <div class="d m10" style="border-style:none;position:absolute;left:474.205444px;bottom:158.174393px;width:107.713000px;height:11.008000px;background-color:rgba(255,255,255,0.000001);"></div></a>

               <div class="d m10" style="border-style:none;position:absolute;left:655.623879px;bottom:158.174393px;width:19.890000px;height:11.008000px;background-color:rgba(255,255,255,0.000001);"></div></a>
              <a class="l" href="deref/https%3A%2F%2FCRAN.R-project.org%2Fpackage%3Dsp">
               <div class="d m10" style="border-style:none;position:absolute;left:606.269596px;bottom:140.132644px;width:11.452000px;height:11.008000px;background-color:rgba(255,255,255,0.000001);"></div></a>
              <a class="l" href="publication/308288744_tigris_An_R_Package_to_Access_and_Work_with_Geographic_Data_from_the_US_Census_Bureau#pfc" data-dest-detail="[12,&quot;XYZ&quot;,74.306,694.091,null]">
               <div class="d m10" style="border-style:none;position:absolute;left:688.826360px;bottom:140.132644px;width:52.137000px;height:11.008000px;background-color:rgba(255,255,255,0.000001);"></div></a>
              <a class="l" href="publication/308288744_tigris_An_R_Package_to_Access_and_Work_with_Geographic_Data_from_the_US_Census_Bureau#pfc" data-dest-detail="[12,&quot;XYZ&quot;,74.306,694.091,null]">
               <div class="d m10" style="border-style:none;position:absolute;left:778.832609px;bottom:140.132644px;width:20.230000px;height:11.008000px;background-color:rgba(255,255,255,0.000001);"></div></a>

           </div> 
           <div class="pdf-viewer-page"> 
            <div id="pf2" class="pf w0 h0" data-page-no="2">
             <div class="pc pc2 w0 h0">
              <div class="bi x0 y0 w1 h1 lazyload" data-bg="profile/Kyle_Walker5/publication/308288744/viewer/AS:407972971859976@1474279744999/background/2.png" style="background-size: contain;"></div>
              <div class="t m0 x0 h2 y1 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls0">
               C
               <span class="fs1 ls1 ws0">ONTRIBUTED RESEARCH ARTICLE<span class="_ _0"> </span></span>
               <span class="ls6">2</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y37 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1e">
               given that they represent Census areal entities; selected geographic features, such as roads, linear
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y38 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1f">
               water features, and landmarks, may be represented as objects of class
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x20 h7 y38 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               SpatialLinesDataFrame
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x21 h6 y38 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               or
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 y39 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               SpatialPointsDataFrame
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x22 h6 y39 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               .
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x23 h7 y39 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               Spatial*DataFrames
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x24 h6 y39 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1f">
               are R objects that represent spatial data as closely
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y3a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws20">
               as possible to regular R data frames, yet also contain information about the feature geometry and
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y3b ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               coordinate system of the data (see 
               <span class="fc1">Bivand et al.</span>
               <span class="ls3">,</span>
               <span class="fc1">2013</span>, for more information).
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 xd h6 y3c ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws21">
               Several R packages provide access to Census geographic and demographic data. The UScensus2000
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y3d ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws22">
               (no longer on CRAN) and
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x8 h5 y3d ff2 fs3 fc1 sc0 ls6">
               UScensus2010
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x25 h6 y3d ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws22">
               packages by Zack Almquist allow for access to several
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y3e ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws23">
               geographic datasets for the 2000 and 2010 Censuses, including blocks, Census tracts, and counties
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y3f ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               (
               <span class="fc1">Almquist</span>
               <span class="ls7">,</span>
               <span class="fc1">2010</span>
               <span class="ws24">).<span class="_ _4"> </span>These datasets can also be linked to demographic data from the 2000 and 2010</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y40 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws25">
               Censuses, which are stored in related, external packages.
               <span class="_ _4"> </span>The
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x26 h5 y40 ff2 fs3 fc1 sc0 ls6">
               USABoundaries
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x27 h6 y40 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws25">
               package similarly
              </div>
              <div class="t m11 x1 h6 y41 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1">
               provides access to some Census geographic boundary ?les such as zip code tabulation areas (ZCT
               <span class="_ _2"></span>As)
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y42 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws26">
               and counties; it also makes available historical boundary ?les dating back to 1629 (
               <span class="fc1">Mullen</span>
               <span class="ls8">,</span>
               <span class="fc1">2015</span>).
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y43 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws27">
               Another R package,
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x28 h5 y43 ff2 fs3 fc1 sc0 ls6">
               choroplethr
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x29 h6 y43 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws2">
               , wraps
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x2a h5 y43 ff2 fs3 fc1 sc0 ls6">
               ggplot2
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x2b h6 y43 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               (
               <span class="fc1 ws7">Wickham</span>
               <span class="ls9">,</span>
               <span class="fc1">2009</span>
               <span class="ws27">) to map data from the US Census</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m12 x1 h6 y44 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsa">
               Bureau’s American Community Survey aggregated to common Census geographies (
               <span class="fc1 ws6">Lamstein and</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y45 ff1 fs3 fc1 sc0 ls6">
               Johnson
               <span class="fc0 lsa">,</span>2015
               <span class="fc0 ws28">).<span class="_ _5"> </span>The purpose of the</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x2c h5 y45 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x2d h6 y45 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws28">
               package is to help R users work with US Census Bureau
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y46 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws29">
               geographic data by granting direct access to the Census shape?les via a simple, uniform interface.
              </div>
              <div class="t m2 x1 h6 y47 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws3">
               Further, as
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x2e h5 y47 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m2 x2f h6 y47 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws3">
               interfaces directly with Census Bureau data stores, it ensures access to high-quality
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y48 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               and up-to-date geographic data for R projects.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h8 y49 ff2 fs5 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               Core functionality of tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m13 x1 h6 y4a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1">
               The core functionality of
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x30 h5 y4a ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m13 x31 h6 y4a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1">
               consists of a series of functions, each corresponding to a single Census
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y4b ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws2a">
               Bureau geography of interest, that grant access to geographic data from the US Census Bureau.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h5 y4c ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x32 h6 y4c ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1c">
               allows R users to obtain both the core TIGER/Line shape?les as well as the Census Bureau’s
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y4d ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws2b">
               Cartographic Boundary Files.
               <span class="_ _3"> </span>Cartographic Boundary Files, following the Census Bureau (2015),
              </div>
              <div class="t m8 x1 h6 y4e ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws6">
               "are simpli?ed representations of selected geographic areas fr
               <span class="_ _2"></span>om the Census Bureau’s MAF/TIGER
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y4f ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               geographic database" (
               <span class="fc1">United States Census Bureau</span>
               <span class="ls3">,</span>
               <span class="fc1">2015</span>).
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 xd h6 y50 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws2b">
               T
               <span class="_ _2"></span>o download geographic data using
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x33 h5 y50 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x34 h6 y50 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws2b">
               , the R user calls the function corresponding to the
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y51 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws2c">
               desired geography
               <span class="_ _2"></span>.
               <span class="_ _7"> </span>For example, to obtain a
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x24 h7 y51 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               SpatialPolygonsDataFrame
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x35 h6 y51 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws2d">
               of US states from the
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y52 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws2e">
               TIGER/Line dataset, the user calls the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x2a h7 y52 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               states
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x24 h6 y52 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws2e">
               function in
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x12 h5 y52 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x36 h6 y52 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws2e">
               , which can then be plotted with
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y53 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws2f">
               the 
               <span class="ff4 fs4 ws30">plot </span>
               <span class="ws0">function from the <span class="ff2 fc1 ws31">sp </span>package, which is loaded by <span class="ff2 ws32">tigris </span>automatically:</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 y54 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               library(tigris)
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 y55 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               us_states &lt;- states()
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 y56 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               plot(us_states)
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 xd h6 y57 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               The
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x7 h7 y57 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               states
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x18 h6 y57 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws34">
               function call instructs
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 xb h5 y57 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 xc h6 y57 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws34">
               to fetch a TIGER/Line shape?le from the US Census
              </div>
              <div class="t m13 x1 h6 y58 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1">
               Bureau that represents the boundaries of the 50 US states, the District of Columbia, and US territories.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h5 y59 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x32 h6 y59 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws35">
               then uses
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x18 h5 y59 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               rgdal
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x19 h6 y59 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws35">
               to load the data into the user’s R session as an object of class
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x37 h7 y59 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               Spatial*DataFrame
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x38 h6 y59 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               .
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 y5a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws36">
               Many functions in
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x39 h5 y5a ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 xf h6 y5a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws36">
               have a parameter,
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x33 h7 y5a ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               cb
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 xa h6 y5a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws36">
               , that if set to
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x3a h7 y5a ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               TRUE
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x3b h6 y5a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws36">
               will direct
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x20 h5 y5a ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x3c h6 y5a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws36">
               to load a cartographic
              </div>
              <div class="t m4 x1 h6 y5b ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsa">
               boundary ?le instead. Cartographic boundary ?les default to a simpli?ed resolution of 1:500,000; in
              </div>
              <div class="t m14 x1 h6 y5c ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws37">
               some cases, as with states, resolutions of 1:5 million and 1:20 million are available. For example, an
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y5d ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws9">
               R user could specify the following modi?cations to the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x3a h7 y5d ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               states
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x26 h6 y5d ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws9">
               function, and retrieve a simpli?ed
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y5e ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               dataset.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 y5f ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               us_states_20m &lt;- states(cb = TRUE, resolution = "20m")
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 y60 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               ri &lt;- us_states[us_states$NAME == "Rhode Island", ]
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 y61 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               ri_20m &lt;- us_states_20m[us_states_20m$NAME == "Rhode Island", ]
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 y62 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               plot(ri)
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 y63 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               plot(ri_20m, border = "red", add = TRUE)
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 xd h6 y64 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws38">
               The plot illustrates some of the differences between the TIGER/Line shape?les and the cartographic
              </div>
              <div class="t m15 x1 h6 y65 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4">
               boundary ?les, in this instance for the state of Rhode Island. The TIGER/Line shape?les are the most
              </div>
              <div class="t m16 x1 h6 y66 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws3">
               detailed datasets in interior areas, and represent the legal boundaries for coastal areas which extend
              </div>
              <div class="t m17 x1 h6 y67 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws6">
               three miles beyond the shoreline. The Cartographic Boundary Files have less detail in interior areas,
              </div>
              <div class="t m4 x1 h6 y68 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws6">
               but are clipped to the shoreline of the United States, which may be preferable for thematic mapping
              </div>
              <div class="t m15 x1 h6 y69 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4">
               but can introduce additional detail for coastal features. A full list of the geographic datasets available
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y6a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws7">
               through
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x2 h5 y6a ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x3d h6 y6a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws39">
               is found in T
               <span class="_ _2"></span>able 1;
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>datasets with an asterisk are available as both TIGER/Line and
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y6b ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               cartographic boundary ?les.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h2 y36 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               The R Journal V
               <span class="_ _2"></span>ol.
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>XX/YY, AAAA 20ZZ
               <span class="_ _6"> </span>ISSN 2073-4859

              <div class="t m0 x0 h2 y1 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls0">
               C
               <span class="fs1 ls1 ws0">ONTRIBUTED RESEARCH ARTICLE<span class="_ _0"> </span></span>
               <span class="ls6">4</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x3f h2 y71 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws3a">
               Family Functions
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x3f h2 y72 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               General area functions
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x25 h2 y72 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws3b">

              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x25 h2 y73 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws3c">

              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x25 h2 y74 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               school_districts; county_subdivisions*; zctas*
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x3f h2 y75 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">

              </div>
              <div class="t m8 x25 h2 y75 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws3d">

              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x25 h2 y76 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">

              <div class="t m0 x3f h2 y77 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               W
               <span class="_ _2"></span>ater functions
               <span class="_ _8"> </span>area_water; linear_water; coastline
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x3f h2 y78 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               Metro area functions
               <span class="_ _9"> </span>core_based_statistical_areas*;
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x25 h2 y79 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws3e">
               combined_statistical_areas*;
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x25 h2 y7a ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               metro_divisions; new_england*; urban_areas*
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x3f h2 y7b ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               T
               <span class="_ _2"></span>ransportation functions
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x25 h2 y7b ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws3f">
               primary_roads; primary_secondary_roads; roads;
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x25 h2 y7c ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               rails
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x3f h2 y7d ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               Native/tribal geometries functions
              </div>
              <div class="t ma x25 h2 y7d ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws3d">
               native_areas*; alaska_native_regional_corporations*;
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x25 h2 y7e ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws3e">
               tribal_block_groups;
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x25 h2 y7f ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               tribal_census_tracts; tribal_subdivisions_national
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x3f h2 y80 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               Other
               <span class="_ _a"> </span>landmarks; military
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h5 y81 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws40">
               T
               <span class="_ _2"></span>able 1:
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x7 h6 y81 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws12">
               Functions available in the tigris package. Functions denoted with an asterisk are also available
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y82 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               as cartographic boundary ?les.
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 xd h6 y83 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws41">
               When Census data are available for download at sub-national levels, they are referenced by
              </div>
              <div class="t me x1 h6 y84 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws17">
               their Federal Information Processing Standard (FIPS) codes, which are codes that uniquely identify
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y85 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws42">
               geographic entities in the Census database.
               <span class="_ _3"> </span>When applicable,
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x26 h5 y85 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1c h6 y85 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws43">
               uses smart state and county
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y86 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws20">
               lookup to simplify the process of data acquisition for R users.
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>This allows users to obtain data by
              </div>
              <div class="t mf x1 h6 y87 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1d">
               supplying the name or postal code of the desired state – along with the name of the desired county
               <span class="_ _2"></span>,
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 y88 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsb">
               when applicable – rather than their FIPS codes. In the following example, the R user fetches roads data
              </div>
              <div class="t m7 x1 h6 y89 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsd">
               for Kalawao County Hawaii, the smallest county in the United States by area, located on the northern
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y8a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               coast of the island of Moloka’i.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 y8b ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               kw_roads &lt;- roads("HI", "Kalawao")
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 y8c ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               plot(kw_roads)
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x8 h6 y8d ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               Figure 3: 
               <span class="ff1">Roads in Kalawao County, Hawaii.</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 xd h6 y8e ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4">
               While many Census shape?les correspond to these common geographic identi?ers in the United
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y8f ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws41">
               States, not all datasets are identi?able in this way
               <span class="_ _2"></span>.
               <span class="_ _1"> </span>A good example is the Zip Code T
               <span class="_ _2"></span>abulation
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h2 y36 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               The R Journal V
               <span class="_ _2"></span>ol.
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>XX/YY, AAAA 20ZZ
               <span class="_ _6"> </span>ISSN 2073-4859
              </div>
             </div>
             <div class="pi" data-data="{&quot;ctm&quot;:[1.646295,0.000000,0.000000,1.646295,0.000000,0.000000]}"></div>
            </div> 
           </div> 
           <div class="pdf-viewer-page"> 
            <div id="pf5" class="pf w0 h0" data-page-no="5">
             <div class="pc pc5 w0 h0">
              <div class="bi x0 y90 w1 hc lazyload" data-bg="profile/Kyle_Walker5/publication/308288744/viewer/AS:407972971859976@1474279744999/background/5.png" style="background-size: contain;"></div>
              <div class="t m0 x0 h2 y1 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls0">
               C
               <span class="fs1 ls1 ws0">ONTRIBUTED RESEARCH ARTICLE<span class="_ _0"> </span></span>
               <span class="ls6">5</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y37 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws44">
               Area (ZCT
               <span class="_ _2"></span>A), a geographic dataset developed by the US Census Bureau to approximate zip codes,
              </div>
              <div class="t m19 x1 h6 y38 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               postal codes used by the United States Postal Service. Social data in the United States are commonly
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y39 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws45">
               distributed at the zip code level, including an example later in this article;
               <span class="_ _4"> </span>however, zip codes
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y3a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws46">
               themselves are not coherent geographic entities, and change frequently
               <span class="_ _2"></span>.
               <span class="_ _4"> </span>ZCTAs, then, function as
              </div>
              <div class="t m1a x1 h6 y3b ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1d">
               proxies for zip codes, and are built from Census blocks in which a plurality of addresses on a given
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y91 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               block have a given zip code (
               <span class="fc1">United States Census Bureau</span>
               <span class="ls3">,</span>
               <span class="fc1">2016b</span>).
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 xd h6 y3d ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsf">
               ZCTAs commonly cr
               <span class="_ _2"></span>oss county lines and even cross state lines in certain instances; as such, the US
              </div>
              <div class="t m19 x1 h6 y3e ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws3">
               Census Bureau only makes the entire ZCT
               <span class="_ _2"></span>A dataset of over 33,000 zip codes available for download.
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 y3f ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws47">
               Often, analysts will not need all of these ZCTAs for a given pr
               <span class="_ _b"></span>oject.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x36 h5 y3f ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1c h6 y3f ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws47">
               allows users to subset ZCTAs
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 y40 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1c">
               on load with the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x40 h7 y40 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               starts_with
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x41 h6 y40 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1c">
               parameter, which accepts a vector of strings that contains the beginning
              </div>
              <div class="t m2 x1 h6 y41 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws3">
               digits of the ZCTAs that the analyst wants to load into R. The example below r
               <span class="_ _2"></span>etrieves ZCTAs in the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y42 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               area around Fort W
               <span class="_ _2"></span>orth, Texas.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 y92 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               fw_zips &lt;- zctas(cb = TRUE, starts_with = "761")
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 y93 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               plot(fw_zips)
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x2 h6 y94 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               Figure 4: 
               <span class="ff1">Zip Code Tabulation Areas that start with "761" (near Fort W<span class="_ _2"></span>orth, Texas).</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 xd h6 y95 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws48">
               When 
               <span class="ff2 ws49">tigris </span>
               <span class="ws0">downloads Census shape?les to the R user’s computer, it uses the <span class="ff2 fc1 ws4a">rappdirs </span>package</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y96 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4b">
               to cache the downloads for future access (
               <span class="fc1">Ratnakumar et al.</span>
               <span class="lsb">,</span>
               <span class="fc1">2014</span>).
               <span class="_ _3"> </span>In turn, once the R user has
              </div>
              <div class="t m1b x1 h6 y97 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1d">
               downloaded the Census geographic data,
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x2d h5 y97 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1b x24 h6 y97 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1d">
               will know where to look for it and will not need to
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y98 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4c">
               re-download.
               <span class="_ _4"> </span>To turn of
               <span class="_ _2"></span>f this behavior, a
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x2d h5 y98 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x24 h6 y98 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4c">
               user can set
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x4 h7 y98 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4d">
               options(tigris_use_cache = FALSE)
              </div>
              <div class="t me x1 h6 y99 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1d">
               after loading the package; this will direct
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x33 h5 y99 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t me x42 h6 y99 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1d">
               to download shape?les to a temporary directory on
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y9a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               the user’s computer instead, and load data into R from there.
              </div>
              <div class="t m18 xd h6 y9b ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsf">
               The Census Bureau releases updated TIGER/Line shape?les every year
               <span class="_ _2"></span>, and these yearly updates
              </div>
              <div class="t m4 x1 h6 y9c ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws6">
               are available to
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x18 h5 y9c ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m4 x19 h6 y9c ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               users.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x8 h5 y9c ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m4 x1d h6 y9c ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws6">
               defaults to the 2015 shape?les, which at the time of this writing is
              </div>
              <div class="t m17 x1 h6 y9d ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsa">
               the most recent year available.. However,
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x33 h5 y9d ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m17 x42 h6 y9d ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws6">
               users can supply a different year to a
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x43 h5 y9d ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m17 x44 h6 y9d ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               function
              </div>
              <div class="t md x1 h6 y9e ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1">
               as a named argument to obtain data for a different year; for example,
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1b h7 y9e ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4e">
               year = 2014
              </div>
              <div class="t md x27 h6 y9e ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1">
               in the function call
              </div>
              <div class="t m3 x1 h6 y9f ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4">
               will fetch TIGER/Line shape?les or cartographic boundary ?les from 2014. Additionally, R users can
              </div>
              <div class="t m1c x1 h6 ya0 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsd">
               set this as a global option in their R session by entering the command
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x16 h7 ya0 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               options(tigris_year = 2014)
              </div>
              <div class="t m1c x38 h6 ya0 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               .
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h8 ya1 ff2 fs5 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               Data manipulation with tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 ya2 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws20">
               The primary utility of the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x23 h5 ya2 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x29 h6 ya2 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws20">
               package is for consistent and quick data access for R users with a
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y8e ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4f">
               minimum of code.
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>As
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x45 h5 y8e ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x46 h6 y8e ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4f">
               loads objects of class
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x47 h7 y8e ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               Spatial*
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x12 h6 y8e ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws50">
               from the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x5 h5 y8e ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               sp
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1f h6 y8e ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4f">
               package, data analysis and
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 y8f ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws36">
               visualization using the acquired data can be handled with R’s suite of cartographic and spatial analysis
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h2 y36 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               The R Journal V
               <span class="_ _2"></span>ol.
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>XX/YY, AAAA 20ZZ
               <span class="_ _6"> </span>ISSN 2073-4859
              </div>

             <div class="pc pc6 w0 h0">
              <div class="bi x0 ya3 w1 hd lazyload" data-bg="profile/Kyle_Walker5/publication/308288744/viewer/AS:407972971859976@1474279744999/background/6.png" style="background-size: contain;"></div>
              <div class="t m0 x0 h2 y1 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls0">
               C
               <span class="fs1 ls1 ws0">ONTRIBUTED RESEARCH ARTICLE<span class="_ _0"> </span></span>
               <span class="ls6">6</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y37 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws51">
               packages, which will be addressed later in the article.
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>However,
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x36 h5 y37 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1f h6 y37 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws51">
               does include two functions,
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 y38 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               rbind_tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1b xe h6 y38 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               and
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x48 h7 y38 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               geo_join
              </div>
              <div class="t m1b x8 h6 y38 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1d">
               , to assist with common operations when working with Census Bureau
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y39 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               geographic data: combining datasets with one another, or merging them to tabular data.
              </div>
              <div class="t me xd h6 ya4 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsa">
               Some Census shape?les, like roads, are only available by county; however
               <span class="_ _2"></span>, an R user may want
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 ya5 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws52">
               a roads dataset that represents multiple counties.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x14 h5 ya5 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x15 h6 ya5 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws52">
               has built-in functionality to handle these
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y3c ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws53">
               circumstances.
               <span class="_ _4"> </span>Data loaded into R by
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 xb h5 y3c ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 xc h6 y3c ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws53">
               functions are assigned a special
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x3c h7 y3c ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x49 h6 y3c ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws53">
               attribute that
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 y3d ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws54">
               identi?es the type of geographic data represented by the object. This attribute can be checked with the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y3e ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws55">
               function 
               <span class="ff4 fs4 ws56">tigris_type</span>:
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 ya6 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris_type(kw_roads)
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 ya7 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               [1] "road"
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 xd h6 ya8 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws41">
               Objects with the same
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x8 h7 ya8 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x4a h6 ya8 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws41">
               attributes can then be combined into a single object using the
              </div>
              <div class="t m3 x1 h6 ya9 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               function
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x2 h7 ya9 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               rbind_tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m3 x45 h6 ya9 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4">
               . In the example below, the user loads data for Maui County
               <span class="_ _2"></span>, which comprises
              </div>
              <div class="t m1d x1 h6 yaa ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsa">
               the remainder of the island of Moloka’i as well as the islands of Maui and Lana’i. As the roads data
              </div>
              <div class="t m11 x1 h6 yab ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1">
               do not explicitly contain information about counties, an identifying
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x4b h7 yab ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               county
              </div>
              <div class="t m11 x17 h6 yab ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsf">
               column is speci?ed in the
              </div>
              <div class="t m1d x1 h6 yac ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1d">
               example below
               <span class="_ _2"></span>.
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>The data are then plotted and colored by county; Kalawao County is colored red in
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 yad ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               the ?gure.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yae ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               maui_roads &lt;- roads("HI", "Maui")
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yaf ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               kw_roads$county &lt;- "Kalawao"
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yb0 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               maui_roads$county &lt;- "Maui"
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yb1 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               maui_kw_roads &lt;- rbind_tigris(kw_roads, maui_roads)
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yb2 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               plot(maui_kw_roads, col = c("red", "black")[as.factor(maui_kw_roads$county)])
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x39 h6 yb3 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               Figure 5: 
               <span class="ff1">Roads in Maui County and Kalawao County, Hawaii.</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 xd h6 yb4 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               The
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x7 h7 yb4 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               rbind_tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x4c h6 yb4 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws54">
               function also accepts a list of
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1a h5 yb4 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               sp
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x4d h6 yb4 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws54">
               objects with the same
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x4e h7 yb4 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x4f h6 yb4 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws54">
               attributes. This is
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 yb5 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsb">
               particularly useful in the event that an analyst needs a dataset that covers the United States, but is only
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 yb6 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws57">
               available at sub-national levels.
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>An example of this is the Public Use Microdata Area (PUMA), the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h2 y36 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               The R Journal V
               <span class="_ _2"></span>ol.
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>XX/YY, AAAA 20ZZ
               <span class="_ _6"> </span>ISSN 2073-4859
              </div>
             </div>
             <div class="pi" data-data="{&quot;ctm&quot;:[1.646295,0.000000,0.000000,1.646295,0.000000,0.000000]}"></div>
            </div> 
           </div> 
           <div class="pdf-viewer-page"> 
            <div id="pf7" class="pf w0 h0" data-page-no="7">
             <div class="pc pc7 w0 h0">
              <div class="bi x0 yb7 w1 he lazyload" data-bg="profile/Kyle_Walker5/publication/308288744/viewer/AS:407972971859976@1474279744999/background/7.png" style="background-size: contain;"></div>
              <div class="t m0 x0 h2 y1 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls0">
               C
               <span class="fs1 ls1 ws0">ONTRIBUTED RESEARCH ARTICLE<span class="_ _0"> </span></span>
               <span class="ls6">7</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t mc x1 h6 y37 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               Census geography at which individual-level microdata samples are associated. PUMAs are available
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y38 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               by state in 
               <span class="ff2 ws32">tigris </span>
               <span class="ws58">via the <span class="ff4 fs4 ws59">pumas </span></span>function; however, an analyst will commonly want PUMA geography
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y39 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws11">
               for the entire United States to facilitate national-level analyses.
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>In this example,
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x27 h7 y39 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               rbind_tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x50 h6 y39 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               can
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y3a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws5a">
               be used with
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 xe h7 y3a ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               lapply
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x19 h6 y3a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsc">
               to fetch PUMA datasets for each state and then combine them into a dataset
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y3b ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               covering the continental United States.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 xd h5 y3c ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x3e h6 y3c ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsb">
               includes a built-in data frame named
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x51 h7 y3c ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               fips_codes
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x15 h6 y3c ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsb">
               that used to match state and county names
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 y3d ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1">
               with Census FIPS codes in the various functions in the package. It can also be used to generate vectors
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 y3e ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws5b">
               of codes to be passed to
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x45 h5 y3e ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x46 h6 y3e ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws5b">
               functions as in this example, so that the analyst does not have to generate
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y3f ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               the full list of state codes by hand.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yb8 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               us_states &lt;- unique(fips_codes$state)[1:51]
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yb9 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               continental_states &lt;- us_states[!us_states %in% c("AK", "HI")]
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yba ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               us_pumas &lt;- rbind_tigris(
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x52 h7 ybb ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               lapply(
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x53 h7 ybc ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               continental_states, function(x) {
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x54 h7 ybd ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               pumas(state = x, cb = TRUE)
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x53 h7 ybe ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               }
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x52 h7 ybf ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               )
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yc0 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               )
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yc1 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               plot(us_pumas)
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h5 yc2 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws53">
               Figure 6:
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x3e h6 yc2 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws5c">
               Public Use Microdata Areas (PUMAs) for the continental United States, generated with
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 yc3 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws56">
               rbind_tigris
               <span class="ff1 fs3">.</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 xd h6 yc4 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws5d">
               The above code directs R to iterate through the state codes for the continental United States,
              </div>
              <div class="t me x1 h6 yc5 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1d">
               fetching PUMA geography for each state and storing it in a list which
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1c h7 yc5 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               rbind_tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t me x43 h6 yc5 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1d">
               then combines
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 yc6 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               into a continental PUMA dataset.
              </div>
              <div class="t m8 xd h6 yc7 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws6">
               The other data manipulation function in
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 xa h5 yc7 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m8 x47 h6 yc7 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               ,
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1a h7 yc7 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               geo_join
              </div>
              <div class="t m8 x12 h6 yc7 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws6">
               , is designed to assist with the common
              </div>
              <div class="t m1d x1 h6 yc8 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsa">
               but sometimes-messy process of merging tabular data to US Census Bureau shape?les. Such joined
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 yc9 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4f">
               data can then be used for statistical mapping, such as a choropleth map that shows variation in an
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 yca ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               attribute by the shading of polygons.
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 xd h6 ycb ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws5e">
               In the example below
               <span class="_ _2"></span>,
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>an analyst uses functions in
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x55 h5 ycb ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x3b h6 ycb ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws5e">
               to help create a choropleth map that
              </div>
              <div class="t md x1 h6 ycc ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws54">
               shows how the areas represented by legislators in the T
               <span class="_ _2"></span>exas State House of Representatives, the lower
              </div>
              <div class="t m19 x1 h6 ya2 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws3">
               house of the T
               <span class="_ _2"></span>exas state legislature, vary by political party. By convention in the United States, areas
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 y8e ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws5f">
               represented by members of the Republican Party are shaded in red, and ar
               <span class="_ _2"></span>eas represented by members
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y8f ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               of the Democratic Party are shaded in blue.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h2 y36 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               The R Journal V
               <span class="_ _2"></span>ol.
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>XX/YY, AAAA 20ZZ

              <div class="t m0 x0 h2 y1 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls0">

               <span class="fs1 ls1 ws0">ONTRIBUTED RESEARCH ARTICLE<span class="_ _0"> </span></span>
               <span class="ls6">8</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m19 xd h6 y37 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws3">
               T
               <span class="_ _2"></span>o accomplish this, the analyst loads in a CSV containing information on party representation in
              </div>
              <div class="t m5 x1 h6 y38 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsa">
               T
               <span class="_ _2"></span>exas by legislative district, and uses the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x56 h7 y38 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               state_legislative_districts
              </div>
              <div class="t m5 x20 h6 y38 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1d">
               function to retrieve bound-
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 y39 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws60">
               aries for the legislative districts.
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>The two datasets can then be joined with
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1c h7 y39 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               geo_join
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x37 h6 y39 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws60">
               . The
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>?rst argument
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 y3a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws54">
               in the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x32 h7 y3a ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               geo_join
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x18 h6 y3a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws54">
               call represents the object of class
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x42 h7 y3a ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               Spatial*DataFrame
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x4b h6 y3a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws54">
               ; the second argument represents
              </div>
              <div class="t m11 x1 h6 y3b ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsf">
               a regular R data frame. The third and fourth arguments specify the columns in the spatial data frame
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y91 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4">
               and regular data frame, respectively
               <span class="_ _2"></span>, to be used to match the rows; if the names of these columns are
              </div>
              <div class="t m12 x1 h6 yce ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1d">
               the same, that name can be passed as a named argument to the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x57 h7 yce ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               by
              </div>
              <div class="t m12 x13 h6 yce ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws37">
               parameter, which is unused her
               <span class="_ _2"></span>e.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 ycf ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               Once the two datasets are joined, they can be visualized with 
               <span class="ff2 ws31">sp </span>plotting functions.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yd0 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               df &lt;- read.csv("http://personal.tcu.edu/kylewalker/data/txlege.csv",
              </div>

              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yd3 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               txlege &lt;- geo_join(districts, df, "NAME", "District")
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yd4 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               txlege$color &lt;- ifelse(txlege$Party == "R", "red", "blue")
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yd5 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               plot(txlege, col = txlege$color)
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yd6 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               legend("topright", legend = c("Republican", "Democrat"),
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x7 h7 yd7 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               fill = c("red", "blue"))

              <div class="t m0 x1 h5 yd8 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws3">

              <div class="t m0 x1 h8 ydf ff2 fs5 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               Analytic visualization in R using data obtained with tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t mb x1 h6 ye0 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               T
               <span class="_ _2"></span>o this point, this paper has employed simpli?ed examples to demonstrate the functionality of
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x58 h5 ye0 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t mb x38 h6 ye0 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               ;
              </div>
              <div class="t m20 x1 h6 ye1 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4">
               the following scenario combines these examples into an applied analytic and visualization work?ow
               <span class="_ _2"></span>.
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 ye2 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws53">
               The goal here is to show how
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x59 h5 ye2 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x5a h6 ye2 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws53">
               ?ts in with a broader spatial analysis work?ow in R. R has a
              </div>
              <div class="t m21 x1 h6 ye3 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsd">
               plethora of packages available for geographic visualization and spatial analysis; for analysts working
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h2 y36 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               The R Journal V
               <span class="_ _2"></span>ol.
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>XX/YY, AAAA 20ZZ
               <span class="_ _6"> </span>ISSN 2073-4859
              </div>
              <a class="l" href="deref/https%3A%2F%2Fwww.texastribune.org%2Fdirectory%2F">
               <div class="d m10" style="border-style:none;position:absolute;left:632.088443px;bottom:388.548707px;width:113.113000px;height:11.008000px;background-color:rgba(255,255,255,0.000001);"></div></a>
