           <div class="pdf-viewer-page"> 
            <div id="pf9" class="pf w0 h0" data-page-no="9">
             <div class="pc pc9 w0 h0">
              <div class="bi x0 y0 w1 h1 lazyload" data-bg="profile/Kyle_Walker5/publication/308288744/viewer/AS:407972971859976@1474279744999/background/9.png" style="background-size: contain;"></div>
              <div class="t m0 x0 h2 y1 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls0">
               C
               <span class="fs1 ls1 ws0">ONTRIBUTED RESEARCH ARTICLE<span class="_ _0"> </span></span>
               <span class="ls6">9</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m11 x1 h6 y37 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1">
               with United States geographies,
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x5b h5 y37 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m11 x9 h6 y37 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1">
               can contribute to the analytic process by providing ample data
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y38 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               access with a minimum of code, and without having to retrieve datasets outside of R.
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 xd h6 ye4 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws62">
               This example demonstrates how to create metropolitan area maps of taxation data from the United
              </div>
              <div class="t mf x1 h6 ya4 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws17">
               States Internal Revenue Service (IRS), which are made available at the zip code level (
               <span class="fc1 ws37">United States</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 ya5 ff1 fs3 fc1 sc0 ls6 ws63">
               Internal Revenue Service
               <span class="fc0 lsc">,</span>2015
               <span class="fc0">).<span class="_ _3"> </span>As discussed earlier<span class="_ _2"></span>,<span class="_ _5"> </span>zip codes are not physical areas but rather</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m1a x1 h6 y3c ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1d">
               designations given by the United States Postal Service (USPS) to guide mail routes; as such, ZCT
               <span class="_ _2"></span>As
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y3d ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               will be used instead, and accessed with the 
               <span class="ff4 fs4 ws64">zctas </span>function.
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 xd h6 ye5 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws5f">
               As ZCTAs do not have a clear corr
               <span class="_ _2"></span>espondence between their boundaries and those of other Census
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 ye6 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws37">
               units, ZCTA boundaries will commonly cr
               <span class="_ _2"></span>oss those of metropolitan areas, which are county-based.
              </div>
              <div class="t m22 x1 h6 ye7 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws7">
               However,
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x5c h5 ye7 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m22 x18 h6 ye7 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsd">
               provides programmatic access to metropolitan area boundaries as well, which in turn
              </div>
              <div class="t m22 x1 h6 ye8 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsd">
               can be used to identify intersecting ZCTAs thr
               <span class="_ _2"></span>ough spatial overlay with the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x17 h5 ye8 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               sp
              </div>
              <div class="t m22 x35 h6 ye8 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsd">
               package. The resultant
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 ye9 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               spatial data can then be merged to data from the IRS and visualized.
              </div>
              <div class="t m23 xd h6 yea ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsd">
               Such a work?ow could resemble the following. An analyst reads in raw data from the IRS website
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 yd3 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws65">
               as an R data frame, and uses the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x5b h5 yd3 ff2 fs3 fc1 sc0 ls6">
               dplyr
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x9 h6 yd3 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws65">
               package (
               <span class="fc1 ws62">Wickham and Francois</span>
               <span class="lsd">,</span>
               <span class="fc1">2015</span>) to subset the data frame
              </div>
              <div class="t m9 x1 h6 yeb ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4">
               and identify the average total income reported to the IRS by zip code in thousands of dollars in 2013,
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 yd4 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws66">
               assigning it to the variable
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x5d h7 yd4 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               df
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x46 h6 yd4 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws66">
               . In the original IRS dataset,
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x3 h7 yd4 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               A02650
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x57 h6 yd4 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws66">
               represents the aggregate total income
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 yec ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws15">
               reported to the IRS by zip code in thousands of dollars, and
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x3b h7 yec ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               N02650
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x5 h6 yec ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws15">
               represents the number of tax
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 yd5 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               returns that reported total income in that zip code.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yed ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               library(dplyr)
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yee ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               library(stringr)
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yef ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               library(readr)
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yf0 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               # Read in the IRS data
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yf1 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               zip_data &lt;- "https://www.irs.gov/pub/irs-soi/13zpallnoagi.csv"
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yf2 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               df &lt;- read_csv(zip_data) %&gt;%
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x52 h7 yf3 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               mutate(zip_str = str_pad(as.character(ZIPCODE), width = 5,
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x31 h7 yf4 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               side = "left", pad = "0"),
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x5c h7 yf5 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               incpr = A02650 / N02650) %&gt;%
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x52 h7 yf6 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               select(zip_str, incpr)
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 xd h6 yf7 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1b">
               The analyst then de?nes a function that will leverage
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x3 h5 yf7 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x4 h6 yf7 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1b">
               to read in Census ZCT
               <span class="_ _2"></span>A and metropoli-
              </div>
              <div class="t md x1 h6 yf8 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1">
               tan area datasets as objects of class
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1d h7 yf8 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               SpatialPolygonsDataFrame
              </div>
              <div class="t md x4 h6 yf8 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1">
               , and return the ZCT
               <span class="_ _2"></span>As that intersect a
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 yf9 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               given metropolitan area as de?ned by the analyst.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yfa ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               library(tigris)
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yfb ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               library(sp)
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yfc ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               # Write function to get ZCTAs for a given metro
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yfd ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               get_zips &lt;- function(metro_name) {
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x52 h7 yfe ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               zips &lt;- zctas(cb = TRUE)
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x52 h7 yff ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               metros &lt;- core_based_statistical_areas(cb = TRUE)
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x52 h7 y100 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               # Subset for specific metro area
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x52 h7 y101 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               # (be careful with duplicate cities like "Washington")
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x52 h7 y102 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               my_metro &lt;- metros[grepl(sprintf("^%s", metro_name),
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x31 h7 y103 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               metros$NAME, ignore.case = TRUE), ]
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x52 h7 y104 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               # Find all ZCTAs that intersect the metro boundary
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x52 h7 y105 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               metro_zips &lt;- over(my_metro, zips, returnList = TRUE)[[1]]
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x52 h7 y106 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               my_zips &lt;- zips[zips$ZCTA5CE10 %in% metro_zips$ZCTA5CE10, ]
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x52 h7 y107 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               # Return those ZCTAs
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x52 h7 y108 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               return(my_zips)
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 y109 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               }
              </div>
              <div class="t m3 xd h6 y10a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               The analyst can then fetch ZCTA geography for a given metr
               <span class="_ _2"></span>opolitan area, which in this example
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 y10b ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsa">
               will be Dallas-Fort W
               <span class="_ _2"></span>orth, Texas, and merge the IRS income data to it with
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1f h7 y10b ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               geo_join
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x27 h6 y10b ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsa">
               . For visualization,
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y10c ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws50">
               this example uses the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x4c h5 y10c ff2 fs3 fc1 sc0 ls6">
               tmap
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x8 h6 y10c ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws50">
               package (
               <span class="fc1 ws7">T<span class="_ _2"></span>ennekes<span class="fc0 lse">,</span>2015<span class="fc0 ws2">), an excellent option for creating high-quality</span></span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y10d ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws67">
               cartographic products in R, to create a choropleth map. To provide spatial refer
               <span class="_ _2"></span>ence to the Census
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h2 y36 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               The R Journal V
               <span class="_ _2"></span>ol.
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>XX/YY, AAAA 20ZZ
               <span class="_ _6"> </span>ISSN 2073-4859
              </div>

               <div class="d m10" style="border-style:none;position:absolute;left:726.582493px;bottom:1197.398215px;width:55.715000px;height:11.008000px;background-color:rgba(255,255,255,0.000001);"></div></a>

               tracts on the map, major roads obtained with the

              </div>

              </div>

              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x52 h7 y114 ff4 fs4 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws33">
               tm_fill("incpr", style = "quantile", n = 7, palette = "Greens", title = "") +
              </div>

              </div>

               tm_lines(col = "darkgrey") +
              </div>

               tm_layout(bg.color = "ivory",
              </div>

              </div>

              <div class="t m1 xd h6 y120 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws18">
               Given that both geographic data obtained through
              </div>

               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x4 h6 y120 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws18">
               and the IRS data are available for the
              </div>
              <div class="t mc x1 h6 y121 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               entire country
               <span class="_ _2"></span>, an R developer could extend this example and create a web application that generates
              </div>
              <div class="t m18 x1 h6 y122 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsf">
               interactive income maps based on user input with the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x4d h5 y122 ff2 fs3 fc1 sc0 ls6">

               <span class="fc1">Chang et al.</span>
               <span class="lsf">,</span>
               <span class="fc1">2016</span>). Below is an
              </div>
              <div class="t m23 x1 h6 y123 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws54">

              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h7 yc7 ff4 fs4 fc1 sc0 ls6 ws56">
               zip-income
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x60 h6 yc7 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws47">
               ; the code for the application can be viewed at
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x55 h7 yc7 ff4 fs4 fc1 sc0 ls6 ws56">
               http://github.com/walkerke/tigris-zip-
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 yc8 ff4 fs4 fc1 sc0 ls6 ws56">
               income
               <span class="ff1 fs3 fc0">.</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 xd h6 y124 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws68">
               In the application, the user selects a metropolitan area from the drop-down menu, instructing
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y125 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws1d">

              <div class="t m11 x1 h6 ycb ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsf">

              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1f h5 ycb ff2 fs3 fc1 sc0 ls6">
               lea?et
              </div>
              <div class="t m11 x61 h6 ycb ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsf">
               package (
               <span class="fc1 ws1">Cheng and</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 ycc ff1 fs3 fc1 sc0 ls6">
               Xie
               <span class="fc0 ls10">,</span>2015
               <span class="fc0 ws69">).<span class="_ _5"> </span>The application uses the same process described above for the static map to subset the</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 ya2 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws6a">
               data; in this instance, however, the Shiny server makes these computations on-the-?y in response
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y8e ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws28">
               to user input.
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>In the ?gure, the Los Angeles, California metropolitan area is selected; however, all
              </div>

               metropolitan areas in the United States are available to users of the application. While both of these

              <div class="bi x0 y126 w1 h11 lazyload" data-bg="profile/Kyle_Walker5/publication/308288744/viewer/AS:407972971859976@1474279744999/background/11.png" style="background-size: contain;"></div>
              <div class="t m0 x0 h2 y1 ff1 fs0 fc0 sc0 ls0">
               C
               <span class="fs1 ls1 ws0">ONTRIBUTED RESEARCH ARTICLE<span class="_ _c"> </span></span>
               <span class="ls6">11</span>
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h5 y127 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               Figure 9:
              </div>
              <div class="t m3 x2 h6 y127 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4">
               Interactive Lea?et map of average reported total income to the Internal Revenue Service by
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y128 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               zip code for the Los Angeles, California metropolitan area in 2013, built in Shiny
               <span class="_ _2"></span>.
              </div>
              <div class="t m15 x1 h6 y129 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsf">
               cartographic examples require considerable R infrastructure to process the data and ultimately cr
               <span class="_ _2"></span>eate
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y12a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws11">
               the visualizations,
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x48 h5 y12a ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x22 h6 y12a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws11">
               plays a key role in each by providing direct access to reliable spatial data
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y12b ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               programmatically from R.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h8 y12c ff2 fs5 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               Conclusion
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y12d ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsa">
               This paper has summarized the functionality of the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x62 h5 y12d ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x5f h6 y12d ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsa">
               package for retrieving and working with
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 y12e ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws6b">
               shape?les from the United States Census Bureau. Access to high-quality spatial data is essential for the
              </div>
              <div class="t m1c x1 h6 y12f ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws54">
               geospatial analyst, but can be dif?cult to access. For R users working on projects that can bene?t from
              </div>
              <div class="t m8 x1 h6 y130 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsa">
               United States Census Bureau data,
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x4a h5 y130 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m8 x2a h6 y130 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws6">
               provides direct access to the Census Bureau’s TIGER/Line
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y131 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws6a">
               and cartographic boundary ?les using a simple and consistent API. In turn, tasks such as looking
              </div>
              <div class="t m25 x1 h6 y132 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               up FIPS codes to identify the correct datasets to download or combining several Census datasets are
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y133 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               reduced to a few lines of R code in 
               <span class="ff2 ws7">tigris</span>.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 xd h6 y134 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws3">
               More signi?cantly
               <span class="_ _2"></span>, the utility of 
               <span class="ff2 ws6c">tigris </span>is exempli?ed when included in a larger geospatial project
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y135 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws6d">
               that incorporates US Census data, such as the static and interactive maps of IRS data included in
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y136 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws4b">
               this article.
               <span class="_ _3"> </span>These examples illustrate some clear advantages that R has over traditional desktop
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y137 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws6e">
               Geographic Information Systems software for geographic analysis and visualization.
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>To create an
              </div>
              <div class="t m15 x1 h6 y138 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsf">
               interactive application showing IRS data by zip code as in Figure 9, a GIS analyst would traditionally
              </div>
              <div class="t m26 x1 h6 y139 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsa">
               have to search out and download the data from the web; load it into a desktop GIS for merging and
              </div>
              <div class="t m15 x1 h6 y13a ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsf">
               calculating new columns; publish the data to a server; and build the application with a web mapping
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y13b ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws57">
               client and web application framework, often requiring several software applications. As shown in
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y13c ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws44">
               this article, this entire process now can take place inside of an R script, helping ensure quality and
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y13d ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws6f">
               reproducibility
               <span class="_ _2"></span>.
               <span class="_ _5"> </span>For projects that require US Census Bureau geographic data,
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x3c h5 y13d ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x63 h6 y13d ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws6f">
               aims to ?t well
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h6 y13e ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws0">
               within these types of work?ows.
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x1 h8 y13f ff2 fs5 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               Acknowledgments
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x1 h6 y140 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsb">
               I am indebted to Bob Rudis, whose key contributions to the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x64 h5 y140 ff2 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6">
               tigris
              </div>
              <div class="t m6 x57 h6 y140 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 wsb">
               package were essential in improving
              </div>
              <div class="t m1 x1 h6 y141 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws70">
               its functionality
               <span class="_ _2"></span>.
               <span class="_ _3"> </span>I would also like to thank Eli Knaap, who encouraged me to write the package;
              </div>
              <div class="t m12 x1 h9 y142 ff1 fs3 fc0 sc0 ls6 ws37">
               Hadley Wickham for writing 
               <span class="ff3">R Packages </span>and the
              </div>
              <div class="t m0 x24 h5 y142 ff2 fs3 fc1 sc0 ls6">
               devtools
              </div>

                   <div class="publication-author-list" data-reactid="31">
                    <span class="publication-author" data-reactid="32"><img class="img-circle" src="https://c5.rgstatic.net/m/4951093203564/images/template/default/profile/profile_default_s.jpg" alt="Hadley Wickham" title="Hadley Wickham" height="20px" width="20px" style="height:20px;" data-reactid="33"><a href="scientific-contributions/2080184075_Hadley_Wickham" class="publication-author-link ga-publication-author-link" data-reactid="34"><span data-reactid="35">Hadley Wickham</span></a></span>

                  <li class="c-list-item li-publication no-preview" data-reactid="40">
                   <div class="indent-right" data-reactid="41"></div>
                   <!-- react-text: 42 -->
                   <!-- /react-text -->
                   <div style="margin-top:-2px;" data-reactid="43">
                    <h5 class="pub-type-and-title" data-reactid="44"><a class="js-publication-title-link ga-publication-item" href="publication/280016625_US_census_spatial_and_demographic_data_in_R_The_UScensus2000_suite_of_packages" data-reactid="45"><span class="publication-title js-publication-title" data-reactid="46">US census spatial and demographic data in R: The UScensus2000 suite of packages</span></a></h5>
                   </div>
                   <div class="abstract" data-reactid="47">
                    <span class="shorten" data-reactid="48"><a href="#" data-reactid="49">
                      <!-- react-text: 50 -->
                      <!-- /react-text -->
                      <!-- react-text: 51 -->[Show abstract] 
                      <!-- /react-text --></a></span>
                    <span class="full" data-reactid="52"><a href="#" data-reactid="53">
                      <!-- react-text: 54 -->
                      <!-- /react-text -->
                      <!-- react-text: 55 -->[Hide abstract] 
                      <!-- /react-text --></a>
                     <!-- react-text: 56 -->
                     <!-- /react-text --><span data-reactid="57"><strong data-reactid="58">ABSTRACT:</strong>
                      <!-- react-text: 59 --> 
                      <!-- /react-text -->
                      <!-- react-text: 60 -->The US Decennial Census is arguably the most important data set for social science research in the United States. The UScensus2000 suite of packages allows for convenient handling of the 2000 US Census spatial and demographic data. The goal of this article is to showcase the UScensus2000 suite of packages for R, to describe the data contained within these packages, and to demonstrate the helper functions provided for handling this data. The UScensus2000 suite is comprised of spatial and demographic data for the 50 states and Washington DC at four different geographic levels (block, block group, tract, and census designated place). The UScensus2000 suite also contains a number of functions for selecting and aggregating specific geographies or demographic information such as metropolitan statistical areas, counties, etc. These packages rely heavily on the spatial tools developed by Bivand, Pebesma, and G ?omez-Rubio (2008), i.e., the sp and maptools packages. This article will provide the necessary background for working with this data set, helper functions, and finish with an applied spatial statistics example.
                      <!-- /react-text --></span></span>
                   </div>
                   <div class="publication-meta publication-meta" data-reactid="61">
                    <span class="ico-publication-fulltext" data-reactid="62"></span>
                    <span data-reactid="63">
                     <!-- react-text: 64 --> 
                     <!-- /react-text -->

                   <div style="margin-top:-2px;" data-reactid="84">
                    <h5 class="pub-type-and-title" data-reactid="85"><a class="js-publication-title-link ga-publication-item" href="publication/279367378_Applied_Spatial_Data_Analysis_With_R" data-reactid="86"><span class="publication-title js-publication-title" data-reactid="87">Applied Spatial Data Analysis With R</span></a></h5>
                   </div>
                   <div class="abstract" data-reactid="88">
                    <span class="shorten" data-reactid="89"><a href="#" data-reactid="90">
                      <!-- react-text: 91 -->
                      <!-- /react-text -->
                      <!-- react-text: 92 -->[Show abstract] 
                      <!-- /react-text --></a></span>
                    <span class="full" data-reactid="93"><a href="#" data-reactid="94">
                      <!-- react-text: 95 -->
                      <!-- /react-text -->
                      <!-- react-text: 96 -->[Hide abstract] 
                      <!-- /react-text --></a>
                     <!-- react-text: 97 -->
                     <!-- /react-text --><span data-reactid="98"><strong data-reactid="99">ABSTRACT:</strong>
                      <!-- react-text: 100 --> 
                      <!-- /react-text -->
                      <!-- react-text: 101 -->This chapter is concerned with a more detailed explanation of some of the methods that are provided for working with the spatial classes described in Chap. 2. We first consider the question of the spatial support of observations, going on to cover the handling and combination of features using in particular the rgeos package. Next we consider map overlay, also known as spatial join operations, including aggregation, extract operations in the raster package, and spatial sampling.
                      <!-- /react-text --></span></span>
                   </div>

                    <!-- /react-text -->

The tigris package provides a uniform interface\nfor R users to download and work with these shapefiles. Functions in tigris allow R users to request\nCensus geographic datasets using familiar geographic identifiers and return those datasets as objects\nof class Spatial*DataFrame. In turn, tigris ensures consistent and high-quality spatial data for R\nusers\u2019 cartographic and spatial analysis projects that involve US Census data. This article provides\nan overview of the functionality of the tigris package, and concludes with an applied example of a\ngeospatial workflow using data retrieved with Previous studies of RTCs in Trinidad and Tobago were primarily concerned with patterns of drivers use of seat belts, road collisions as a cause of mortality in young men, and the economic burden of road collisions.
